  /** Converts a <button> to look like an <a> tag. */
  .linkify {
    display: inline;
    padding: 0;
    margin: 0;
    border: 0;

    color: var(--chops-link-color);

  }
  a:hover, .linkify:hover {
    text-decoration: underline;
  }
  a.button, .button {
    /* Links that look like buttons. */
    display: inline-flex;
    align-items: center;

    text-decoration: none;

  textarea, select, input {

  }
  /* Note: decoupling heading levels from styles is useful for

        }

          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;

        }

        }

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to <a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.</p>

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>

        <p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

### Report description



<span class="line"><!---->### Report description<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





Generic CORS bypass that enables Cross-Site-Tracing (XST)



<span class="line"><!---->Generic CORS bypass that enables Cross-Site-Tracing (XST)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





---



<span class="line"><!---->---<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





### Bug location



<span class="line"><!---->### Bug location<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Which product or website have you found a vulnerability in?



<span class="line"><!---->#### Which product or website have you found a vulnerability in?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Google Chrome



<span class="line"><!---->Google Chrome<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Which URL (or repository) have you found the vulnerability in?



<span class="line"><!---->#### Which URL (or repository) have you found the vulnerability in?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





all



<span class="line"><!---->all<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





---



<span class="line"><!---->---<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





### The problem



<span class="line"><!---->### The problem<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Please describe the technical details of the vulnerability



<span class="line"><!---->#### Please describe the technical details of the vulnerability<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





For several years, all the main browsers have all blocked the direct use of the TRACE method through fetch and XMLHttpRequest.



<span class="line"><!---->For several years, all the main browsers have all blocked the direct use of the TRACE method through fetch and XMLHttpRequest.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is because a successful Cross-SiteTracing (XST) attack will expose credentials via authorization headers and cookies protected with httponly attributes. 



<span class="line"><!---->This is because a successful Cross-SiteTracing (XST) attack will expose credentials via authorization headers and cookies protected with httponly attributes. <!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To bypass this restriction you can simply add an "X-Http-Method-Override: TRACE" header.



<span class="line"><!---->To bypass this restriction you can simply add an "X-Http-Method-Override: TRACE" header.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





To be successful, this obviously requires a server that supports the TRACE method, and the X-Http-Method-Override header. If so, then any XSS issue can be leveraged into a full compromise of the session/authentication credentials.



<span class="line"><!---->To be successful, this obviously requires a server that supports the TRACE method, and the X-Http-Method-Override header. If so, then any XSS issue can be leveraged into a full compromise of the session/authentication credentials.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





fetch( '



<span class="line"><!---->fetch( '<!----></span>





https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect"><!---->https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect<!----></a>





',



<span class="line"><!---->',<!----></span>





 {



<span class="line"><!----> {<!----></span>



<br>





   method: 'GET',



<span class="line"><!---->   method: 'GET',<!----></span>



<br>





   mode: 'cors',



<span class="line"><!---->   mode: 'cors',<!----></span>



<br>





   headers: {



<span class="line"><!---->   headers: {<!----></span>



<br>





      'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'



<span class="line"><!---->      'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'<!----></span>



<br>





   }



<span class="line"><!---->   }<!----></span>



<br>





} );



<span class="line"><!---->} );<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Please briefly explain who can exploit the vulnerability, and what they gain when doing so



<span class="line"><!---->#### Please briefly explain who can exploit the vulnerability, and what they gain when doing so<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





An attacker can leverage the XSS/XST to bypass the browser protections and gain access to the session/authentication credentials.



<span class="line"><!---->An attacker can leverage the XSS/XST to bypass the browser protections and gain access to the session/authentication credentials.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





---



<span class="line"><!---->---<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





### The cause



<span class="line"><!---->### The cause<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### What version of Chrome have you found the security issue in?



<span class="line"><!---->#### What version of Chrome have you found the security issue in?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





all



<span class="line"><!---->all<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Is the security issue related to a crash?



<span class="line"><!---->#### Is the security issue related to a crash?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





No



<span class="line"><!---->No<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### Choose the type of vulnerability



<span class="line"><!---->#### Choose the type of vulnerability<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Other



<span class="line"><!---->Other<!----></span>



<br>



<br>



<br>





#### How would you like to be publicly acknowledged for your report?



<span class="line"><!---->#### How would you like to be publicly acknowledged for your report?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





scarlet



<span class="line"><!---->scarlet<!----></span>

Hi,



<span class="line"><!---->Hi,<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





It appears this issue affects all the main browsers, and it also appears that the description above may not be the clearest possible.



<span class="line"><!---->It appears this issue affects all the main browsers, and it also appears that the description above may not be the clearest possible.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





I'll have another go at explaining, which should hopefully clear things up.



<span class="line"><!---->I'll have another go at explaining, which should hopefully clear things up.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So a normal CORS fails because the TRACE method is blocked. This is something inherrent in all the major browsers, and was a deliberate change to stop XST.



<span class="line"><!---->So a normal CORS fails because the TRACE method is blocked. This is something inherrent in all the major browsers, and was a deliberate change to stop XST.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





You can see this in action if you browse to 



<span class="line"><!---->You can see this in action if you browse to <!----></span>





https://www.linkedin.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.linkedin.com"><!---->https://www.linkedin.com<!----></a>





,



<span class="line"><!---->,<!----></span>





 then paste the following into the browser console. You'll see the browser block the request. All good.



<span class="line"><!----> then paste the following into the browser console. You'll see the browser block the request. All good.<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





fetch( '



<span class="line"><!---->fetch( '<!----></span>





https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect"><!---->https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect<!----></a>





',



<span class="line"><!---->',<!----></span>





 {



<span class="line"><!----> {<!----></span>



<br>





      method: 'TRACE',



<span class="line"><!---->      method: 'TRACE',<!----></span>



<br>





      mode: 'cors',



<span class="line"><!---->      mode: 'cors',<!----></span>



<br>





      cache: 'no-store'



<span class="line"><!---->      cache: 'no-store'<!----></span>



<br>





} ).then( response => { console.log( response ) } ) 



<span class="line"><!---->} ).then( response =&gt; { console.log( response ) } ) <!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





Now instead, paste in the following. The CORS succeeds and the TRACE overide is sent. Not so good.



<span class="line"><!---->Now instead, paste in the following. The CORS succeeds and the TRACE overide is sent. Not so good.<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





fetch( '



<span class="line"><!---->fetch( '<!----></span>





https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect"><!---->https://realtime.www.linkedin.com/realtime/connect<!----></a>





',



<span class="line"><!---->',<!----></span>





 {



<span class="line"><!----> {<!----></span>



<br>





      method: 'GET',



<span class="line"><!---->      method: 'GET',<!----></span>



<br>





      mode: 'cors',



<span class="line"><!---->      mode: 'cors',<!----></span>



<br>





      cache: 'no-store',



<span class="line"><!---->      cache: 'no-store',<!----></span>



<br>





      headers: {



<span class="line"><!---->      headers: {<!----></span>



<br>





            'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'



<span class="line"><!---->            'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'<!----></span>



<br>





      }



<span class="line"><!---->      }<!----></span>



<br>





} ).then( response => { console.log( response ) } ) 



<span class="line"><!---->} ).then( response =&gt; { console.log( response ) } ) <!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





All that is required are three things to leverage this into a working XST attack (which can be used with any XSS to bypass the httponly flags and also gain access to any authentication tokens in the header):



<span class="line"><!---->All that is required are three things to leverage this into a working XST attack (which can be used with any XSS to bypass the httponly flags and also gain access to any authentication tokens in the header):<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





    a server that echos the CORS request headers (there are oodles of these);



<span class="line"><!---->    a server that echos the CORS request headers (there are oodles of these);<!----></span>



<br>





    a server with TRACE enabled (there are also lots of these: people don't consider it an issue any more because CORS should protect it); and



<span class="line"><!---->    a server with TRACE enabled (there are also lots of these: people don't consider it an issue any more because CORS should protect it); and<!----></span>



<br>





    a server that responds to x-http-method-override: TRACE (less of these, but there are still plenty about).



<span class="line"><!---->    a server that responds to x-http-method-override: TRACE (less of these, but there are still plenty about).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Hopefully that helps your triage.



<span class="line"><!---->Hopefully that helps your triage.<!----></span>

To help with the triage, I've run up a full PoC so that it is clear what the problem is, and how it works.



<span class="line"><!---->To help with the triage, I've run up a full PoC so that it is clear what the problem is, and how it works.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





First browse to 



<span class="line"><!---->First browse to <!----></span>





https://xst.scarlet.ae



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://xst.scarlet.ae"><!---->https://xst.scarlet.ae<!----></a>





 so the cookies are set (and you have something sensitive in the headers).



<span class="line"><!----> so the cookies are set (and you have something sensitive in the headers).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Then browse to any other site (such as 



<span class="line"><!---->Then browse to any other site (such as <!----></span>





https://www.google.com



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://www.google.com"><!---->https://www.google.com<!----></a>





)



<span class="line"><!---->)<!----></span>





 so that CORS will be activated.



<span class="line"><!----> so that CORS will be activated.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Then paste the following into the browser developer tools, console tab:



<span class="line"><!---->Then paste the following into the browser developer tools, console tab:<!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>





fetch( '



<span class="line"><!---->fetch( '<!----></span>





https://xst.scarlet.ae/



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://xst.scarlet.ae/"><!---->https://xst.scarlet.ae/<!----></a>





',



<span class="line"><!---->',<!----></span>





 {



<span class="line"><!----> {<!----></span>



<br>





      method: 'POST',



<span class="line"><!---->      method: 'POST',<!----></span>



<br>





      mode: 'cors',



<span class="line"><!---->      mode: 'cors',<!----></span>



<br>





      cache: 'no-store',



<span class="line"><!---->      cache: 'no-store',<!----></span>



<br>





      credentials: 'include',



<span class="line"><!---->      credentials: 'include',<!----></span>



<br>





      headers: {



<span class="line"><!---->      headers: {<!----></span>



<br>





            'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'



<span class="line"><!---->            'x-http-method-override': 'TRACE'<!----></span>



<br>





      }



<span class="line"><!---->      }<!----></span>



<br>





} )



<span class="line"><!---->} )<!----></span>



<br>





.then( ( response ) => response.text( ) ) 



<span class="line"><!---->.then( ( response ) =&gt; response.text( ) ) <!----></span>



<br>





.then( ( text ) => console.log( text ) ) 



<span class="line"><!---->.then( ( text ) =&gt; console.log( text ) ) <!----></span>



<br>





```



<span class="line"><!---->```<!----></span>



<br>

You should now see the TRACE output, with the request headers, including cookies.



<span class="line"><!---->You should now see the TRACE output, with the request headers, including cookies.<!----></span>

Sorry for the delay! I was OOO.



<span class="line"><!---->Sorry for the delay! I was OOO.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





This is a bit out of my competence. AFAIU, Chrome forbids using several methods:



<span class="line"><!---->This is a bit out of my competence. AFAIU, Chrome forbids using several methods:<!----></span>



<br>





https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:services/network/public/cpp/cors/cors.cc;l=494-499;drc=a432cd59d51281057ba2a2673ca645a9600bb927



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:services/network/public/cpp/cors/cors.cc;l=494-499;drc=a432cd59d51281057ba2a2673ca645a9600bb927"><!---->https://source.chromium.org/chromium/chromium/src/+/main:services/network/public/cpp/cors/cors.cc;l=494-499;drc=a432cd59d51281057ba2a2673ca645a9600bb927<!----></a>



<br>





This includes "CONNECT", "TRACE", "TRACK".



<span class="line"><!---->This includes "CONNECT", "TRACE", "TRACK".<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





TRACE is meant to reflect the requests header. This should be disabled on production servers, because it leads to the disclosure of sensitive information such as internal authentication. To protect weak server, Chrome blocks it by default apparently.



<span class="line"><!---->TRACE is meant to reflect the requests header. This should be disabled on production servers, because it leads to the disclosure of sensitive information such as internal authentication. To protect weak server, Chrome blocks it by default apparently.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So far so good! Then we have "x-http-method-override", which is similar to a hack. It is not supported by Chrome. It is used to bypass web browser built-in protection. On server supporting it, it override the "method" field.



<span class="line"><!---->So far so good! Then we have "x-http-method-override", which is similar to a hack. It is not supported by Chrome. It is used to bypass web browser built-in protection. On server supporting it, it override the "method" field.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





TLDR: In my opinion, everything works the way it is expected. We can't require web browser to block this, because if the goal of developer want to bypass browser protection, they can always add a new header under a different name like "x-http-method-override-2" and so on. This relies on servers to purposefully expose themselves to this kind of security issue.



<span class="line"><!---->TLDR: In my opinion, everything works the way it is expected. We can't require web browser to block this, because if the goal of developer want to bypass browser protection, they can always add a new header under a different name like "x-http-method-override-2" and so on. This relies on servers to purposefully expose themselves to this kind of security issue.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So IMO, we should close this as WontFix. However, as I said, I am not competent here. I would like the last person who touched this behavior to confirm. +@toyoshim, could you please take a look?



<span class="line"><!---->So IMO, we should close this as WontFix. However, as I said, I am not competent here. I would like the last person who touched this behavior to confirm. +@toyoshim, could you please take a look?<!----></span>

Well, there used to be a time that fetch and XMLHttpRequest allowed the CONNECT, TRACE and TRACK methods, but this was changed to stop CORS bypass (and specifically to stop XST attacks).



<span class="line"><!---->Well, there used to be a time that fetch and XMLHttpRequest allowed the CONNECT, TRACE and TRACK methods, but this was changed to stop CORS bypass (and specifically to stop XST attacks).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





And you are right, a specific site could add in CORS support for an X-Cheesecake-Method header, which would allow them to do as they wished. But I think the important point to consider is that this would be intentional, and specific only to themselves.



<span class="line"><!---->And you are right, a specific site could add in CORS support for an X-Cheesecake-Method header, which would allow them to do as they wished. But I think the important point to consider is that this would be intentional, and specific only to themselves.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





With the generic headers outlined above, the support for these is already inherent in many app platforms, and enabled by default. In fact, I’d say that the vast majority of web sites have this issue today: an unrestricted CORS implementation, that allows any origin, with credentials, and the header overrides.



<span class="line"><!---->With the generic headers outlined above, the support for these is already inherent in many app platforms, and enabled by default. In fact, I’d say that the vast majority of web sites have this issue today: an unrestricted CORS implementation, that allows any origin, with credentials, and the header overrides.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Due to the CORS protections, many sites no-longer consider TRACE to be an issue, and so are lax about removing the functionality.



<span class="line"><!---->Due to the CORS protections, many sites no-longer consider TRACE to be an issue, and so are lax about removing the functionality.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





That said, there are far less servers that actually respond to the TRACE method via the override headers, but they are still out there too.



<span class="line"><!---->That said, there are far less servers that actually respond to the TRACE method via the override headers, but they are still out there too.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Fixing the override headers seems to make sense in the browser, in the same way that fixing the TRACE method did too: it’s a global fix.



<span class="line"><!---->Fixing the override headers seems to make sense in the browser, in the same way that fixing the TRACE method did too: it’s a global fix.<!----></span>

The core of what the issue is, is that this is an oversight in the WHATWG spec for fetch. If the override headers were listed in 



<span class="line"><!---->The core of what the issue is, is that this is an oversight in the WHATWG spec for fetch. If the override headers were listed in <!----></span>





https://fetch.spec.whatwg.org/#forbidden-header-name



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://fetch.spec.whatwg.org/#forbidden-header-name"><!---->https://fetch.spec.whatwg.org/#forbidden-header-name<!----></a>





 then we probably wouldn't be having this conversation ;)



<span class="line"><!----> then we probably wouldn't be having this conversation ;)<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





As it stands, there are a lot of servers that implement a relatively relaxed CORS. From a brief anaylsys through those with a safe harbour scheme, probably 90% have at least one URI that enables a CORS preflight with credentials, and also allows the override headers. That's a lot of servers.



<span class="line"><!---->As it stands, there are a lot of servers that implement a relatively relaxed CORS. From a brief anaylsys through those with a safe harbour scheme, probably 90% have at least one URI that enables a CORS preflight with credentials, and also allows the override headers. That's a lot of servers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





On top of this, a large percentage of these also have URIs that respond to the override headers, so that you can send a GET request, but actually flip it to a POST, DELETE or indeed a TRACE.



<span class="line"><!---->On top of this, a large percentage of these also have URIs that respond to the override headers, so that you can send a GET request, but actually flip it to a POST, DELETE or indeed a TRACE.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Although the examples I've given previously are for TRACE, that is mostly because that is the aspect I have been working on (and indeed allows access to credentials and cookies, bypassing the httponly flag).



<span class="line"><!---->Although the examples I've given previously are for TRACE, that is mostly because that is the aspect I have been working on (and indeed allows access to credentials and cookies, bypassing the httponly flag).<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





So as it stands, for a server with an open CORS and also responds to the override headers, you can bypass the CORS method restriction, and deliver a POST (or TRACE) when only GET has been allowed.



<span class="line"><!---->So as it stands, for a server with an open CORS and also responds to the override headers, you can bypass the CORS method restriction, and deliver a POST (or TRACE) when only GET has been allowed.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





That bit is the CORS bypass.



<span class="line"><!---->That bit is the CORS bypass.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Do you chaps have contacts within the WHATWG team? Fixing the standard seems sensible to me.



<span class="line"><!---->Do you chaps have contacts within the WHATWG team? Fixing the standard seems sensible to me.<!----></span>

https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg"><!---->https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg<!----></a>





 can be used for cross-browser discussion.



<span class="line"><!----> can be used for cross-browser discussion.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





FWIW, I tend to agree that this is not a bug in CORS or browsers, but this would not be the first time we do something to be nice for servers.



<span class="line"><!---->FWIW, I tend to agree that this is not a bug in CORS or browsers, but this would not be the first time we do something to be nice for servers.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Mike raises a good point though that some websites might well be relying on these `X-` method override headers to do something useful and blocking them would end up breaking that.



<span class="line"><!---->Mike raises a good point though that some websites might well be relying on these `X-` method override headers to do something useful and blocking them would end up breaking that.<!----></span>

Well, I agree that it's not a bug as such (the browsers implement the standard as it is), but it is still a security issue, isn't it?



<span class="line"><!---->Well, I agree that it's not a bug as such (the browsers implement the standard as it is), but it is still a security issue, isn't it?<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If the goal of CORS is to limit the methods sent to the endpoint, then this is clearly a mechanism for bypassing the limit.



<span class="line"><!---->If the goal of CORS is to limit the methods sent to the endpoint, then this is clearly a mechanism for bypassing the limit.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In practice, the issue is widespread:



<span class="line"><!---->In practice, the issue is widespread:<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





A lot of CORS endpoints respond to the preflight request with a specific origin and method header, but often just parrot-back the contents of the request headers field. From my analysis, this applies to something like 90% of the servers in the field. All the vendors. All the major sites.



<span class="line"><!---->A lot of CORS endpoints respond to the preflight request with a specific origin and method header, but often just parrot-back the contents of the request headers field. From my analysis, this applies to something like 90% of the servers in the field. All the vendors. All the major sites.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





Then on top of this, a lot of the web servers and app frameworks also support the override headers by default.



<span class="line"><!---->Then on top of this, a lot of the web servers and app frameworks also support the override headers by default.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If you combine those two things, then the CORS restriction for methods isn't effective in practice.



<span class="line"><!---->If you combine those two things, then the CORS restriction for methods isn't effective in practice.<!----></span>

The change is discussed at 



<span class="line"><!---->The change is discussed at <!----></span>





https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg"><!---->https://github.com/whatwg/fetch/security/advisories/GHSA-9hrx-wr8g-chvg<!----></a>





 with other browser vendors, but it's a private thread and approved github account is needed to access.



<span class="line"><!----> with other browser vendors, but it's a private thread and approved github account is needed to access.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





In short, we will add the following cases to the forbidden request headers.



<span class="line"><!---->In short, we will add the following cases to the forbidden request headers.<!----></span>



<br>





- The header name is one of below



<span class="line"><!---->- The header name is one of below<!----></span>



<br>





  1. X-HTTP-Method



<span class="line"><!---->  1. X-HTTP-Method<!----></span>



<br>





  2. X-HTTP-Method-Override



<span class="line"><!---->  2. X-HTTP-Method-Override<!----></span>



<br>





  3. X-Method-Override



<span class="line"><!---->  3. X-Method-Override<!----></span>



<br>





- AND, the value is one of below (== forbidden methods)



<span class="line"><!---->- AND, the value is one of below (== forbidden methods)<!----></span>



<br>





  1. CONNECT



<span class="line"><!---->  1. CONNECT<!----></span>



<br>





  2. TRACE



<span class="line"><!---->  2. TRACE<!----></span>



<br>





  3. TRACK



<span class="line"><!---->  3. TRACK<!----></span>

I think that behavior no longer falls under the concept of a "forbidden HTTP method", so we'll need to rename the function, and decide if we want to enforce some sort of more general forbidden value concept to it or figure out a reasonable explanation of what this is the only value restriction rule it enforces (e.g., the fetch spec forbids certain values that don't parse using the new fancy header format, I believe).  Anyhow, feel free to take a stab at it, I'll think about it a bit tomorrow.



<span class="line"><!---->I think that behavior no longer falls under the concept of a "forbidden HTTP method", so we'll need to rename the function, and decide if we want to enforce some sort of more general forbidden value concept to it or figure out a reasonable explanation of what this is the only value restriction rule it enforces (e.g., the fetch spec forbids certain values that don't parse using the new fancy header format, I believe).  Anyhow, feel free to take a stab at it, I'll think about it a bit tomorrow.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->*** Boilerplate reminders! ***<!----></span>



<br>





Please do NOT publicly disclose details until a fix has been released to all our users. Early public disclosure may cancel the provisional reward. Also, please be considerate about disclosure when the bug affects a core library that may be used by other products. Please do NOT share this information with third parties who are not directly involved in fixing the bug. Doing so may cancel the provisional reward. Please be honest if you have already disclosed anything publicly or to third parties. Lastly, we understand that some of you are not interested in money. We offer the option to donate your reward to an eligible charity. If you prefer this option, let us know and we will also match your donation - subject to our discretion. Any rewards that are unclaimed after 12 months will be donated to a charity of our choosing.

Hi, not a chap, but I can answer this question. CVEs are issued to security bugs when the fix is shipped in a Stable channel release. The fix was landed on 109 and as a fix for a low-severity issue, it will be released in 109/Stable. A CVE will be added directly to this bug report at that time.



<span class="line"><!---->Hi, not a chap, but I can answer this question. CVEs are issued to security bugs when the fix is shipped in a Stable channel release.         /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }

          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }

          z-index: 999;

           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */

        }

          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }

          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
